Title: Bifurcations for Lagrangian systems and geodesics I

Markdown Content:
# Bifurcations in Lagrangian systems and geodesics I 

Guangcun Lu ∗

Abstract This paper is Part I of a two-part series. We investigate bifurcation phe-nomena in Lagrangian systems with various boundary conditions and constraints, focusing on the interplay between Morse theory and the existence of multiple so-lutions through three principal configurations: Lagrangian trajectories connecting two submanifolds or with endpoints related by an isometry, and brake orbits in La-grangian systems. For each configuration, we establish necessary and sufficient condi-tions for bifurcation using Morse index and nullity techniques, including classification of Rabinowitz-type alternative bifurcation scenarios. For Euler-Lagrange curves em-anating perpendicularly from a submanifold, we develop a unified Morse-theoretic framework that rigorously connects geometric focal structure (e.g., conjugate points) and analytic bifurcation behavior (e.g., solution branching patterns).

# 1 Introduction and overview of the series 

1.1 Background and motivation 

The study of bifurcation phenomena in variational problems lies at the heart of nonlinear analysis and differential geometry. A fundamental question is to understand how families of solutions to Euler-Lagrange equations change their qualitative behavior as a parameter varies. Classical results, such as the Lyapunov-Schmidt reduction and the celebrated work of Rabinowitz on potential operators, provide abstract frameworks for analyzing such phenomena. In the geometric context, the Morse index theorem elegantly relates the index of a geodesic to its conjugate points, offering a powerful tool for understanding the stability and multiplicity of geodesics in Riemannian geometry. However, extending this elegant theory to more general Lagrangian systems with constraints and various boundary conditions presents significant challenges. While substantial progress has been made for specific cases–such as periodic orbits, geodesics between fixed points, or brake orbits–a unified framework that systematically handles configurations like trajectories connecting two submanifolds, endpoints constrained by an isometry, or generalized periodic solutions has remained less developed. This paper aims to fill this gap by establishing a comprehensive Morse-theoretic approach to bifurcation theory for a broad class of Lagrangian boundary value problems. Our work is motivated by the desire to create a common foundation that not only recovers known results in differential geometry (e.g., bifurcation of geodesics) as special cases but also applies to non-geometric, time-dependent Lagrangian systems. The key insight is to leverage the interplay between the analytic data (Morse index and nullity) and the geometric structure of the problem to derive sharp necessary and sufficient conditions for bifurcation. 

1.2 Main objectives and structure of the series 

This two-part series has the following primary objectives: 1. Part I (Current Paper): To develop a unified Morse-theoretic framework for analyzing bifurcations in Lagrangian systems under three general configurations: 

• Trajectories connecting two submanifolds. 

• Trajectories with endpoints related by an isometry (including generalized periodic solu-tions). Bifurcations for Lagrangian systems and geodesics I 3

• Brake orbits (symmetric periodic trajectories). For each configuration, we establish necessary and sufficient conditions for bifurcation, prove existence theorems, and classify the possible bifurcation scenarios following the tradition of Rabinowitz’s alternatives. 2. Part II (companion paper): To apply the framework developed in Part I to autonomous Lagrangian systems and delve deeper into bifurcation phenomena for geodesics in both Finsler and Riemannian settings, extending the results to broader geometric variational problems. The core technical questions we address in this Part I are precisely formulated in Section 1.4 (see Questions (1)-(3)). The answers, summarized in Theorems 1.4–1.24, provide a complete characterization of bifurcation points in terms of changes in the Morse index and nullity along the trivial branch of solutions. 

1.3 Relation to existing literature 

Our work builds upon and extends several key strands of research. The abstract bifurcation theory for potential operators was pioneered by Rabinowitz [30]. In the context of geodesics, the connection between conjugate points and the Morse index is classical [27, 25]. More re-cent contributions by authors such as Duistermaat [6] (whose index theorem we rely upon in Theorem 3.14), and Piccione et al. [29] on the Maslov index and bifurcation, have significantly advanced the field. The novelty of our approach lies in its systematicity and generality. While previous works often focused on specific settings, we provide a unified treatment that encompasses a wide range of boundary conditions. The techniques employed here combine the abstract critical point theory from [19, 20, 22, 21] with careful geometric reductions to Euclidean spaces, allowing us to handle the technical complexities arising from the manifold setting and constraints. 

1.4 Basic assumptions, conventions, and statement of the research problems 

Throughout, N, Z, and R denote, respectively, the natural numbers, integers, and real num-bers. The symbol τ is a fixed positive number, and Λ denotes the parameter space (typically a real interval or a topological space). 

Assumption 1.0 (Basic assumptions and conventions). Let M be a n-dimensional, connected 

C7 submanifold of RN . Its tangent bundle T M is a C6-smooth manifold of dimension 2 n,whose points are denoted by ( x, v ), with x ∈ M and v ∈ TxM . The bundle projection 

π : T M → M, (x, v ) 7 → x is C6. Let g be a C6 Riemannian metric and Ig a C7 isometry on ( M, g ), i.e., Ig : M → M is C7 and satisfies g(( Ig)∗(u), (Ig)∗(v)) = g(u, v ) for all u, v ∈ T M .(Thus the Christoffel symbols Γ ijk and the exponential map exp : T M → M are C5.) Let N be a submanifold of M × M (specifically, either a product of two submanifolds of M

or the graph of a Riemannian isometry of ( M, g )), and let L : Λ × [0 , τ ] × T M → R be as in Assumption 1.1. The current manuscript focuses on bifurcations research for the following Lagrangian boundary value problem:

(1) Under what conditions there is a bifurcation point ( μ, γ μ) in the above sense? 

(2) What are the necessary (resp. sufficient) condition for a given point ( μ, γ μ) to be a bifur-cation point in the above sense? 

(3) How is the solutions of (1.1) distributed near a bifurcation point ( μ, γ μ) as above ? Roughly speaking, our answers are: 

(a) If Λ is path-connected and there exist two points λ+, λ − ∈ Λ for which the Morse index intervals [m−(Eλ+ , γ λ+ ), m −(Eλ+ , γ λ+ ) + m0(Eλ+ , γ λ+ )] and [m−(Eλ− , γ λ− ), m −(Eλ− , γ λ− ) + m0(Eλ− , γ λ− )] are disjoint, and either m0(Eλ+ , γ λ+ ) = 0 or m0(Eλ− , γ λ− ) = 0, then there exists a point 

μ on any path connecting λ+ to λ− in Λ such that ( μ, γ μ) is a bifurcation point for the family as described as above. 

(b) If Λ is first countable and there exist two points λ+, λ − ∈ Λ in any neighborhood of some 

μ ∈ Λ satisfying the properties as in (a), then ( μ, γ μ) is a bifurcation point. Conversely, for a bifurcation point ( μ, γ μ) it must hold that m0(Eμ, γ μ) > 0. 

(c) If Λ is a real interval, μ ∈ Int(Λ), then the solutions of (1.1) near a bifurcation point ( μ, γ μ)have alternative bifurcations of Rabinowitz’s type (as in [30]) provided that m0(Eλ, γ λ) = 0 for each λ ∈ Λ \ { μ} near μ, and m−(Eλ, γ λ) take, respectively, values m−(Eμ, γ μ) and 

m−(Eμ, γ μ) + m0(Eμ, γ μ) as λ ∈ Λ varies in two deleted half neighborhoods of μ.Bifurcations for Lagrangian systems and geodesics I 5The precise assumptions and main results are organized in the following three subsections. The proofs are built upon the abstract theory from [19, 21], combined with techniques in Appendix A of [21]. As an application, Theorem 1.9 establishes a rigorous one-to-one correspondence between focal points and bifurcation phenomena along Euler-Lagrange curves of (1.15), providing a complete classification of branching behaviors near critical instants.

Assumption 1.7. Let S0 be a boundaryless submanifold of M of dimension dim S0 < dim M ,and let L : [0 , τ ] × T M → R be C3 and fiberwise strictly convex, that is, for each ( t, q, v ) ∈

Theorem 1.9. Under Assumption 1.7, let γ : [0 , τ ] → M be a Euler-Lagrange curve of L

emanating perpendicularly from S0. Then: 

(i) There exist only finitely many S0-focal points along γ.

(ii) If μ ∈ (0 , τ ] is a bifurcation instant for (S0, γ ), then it is a S0-focal point along γ.

(iii) If μ ∈ (0 , τ ) is a S0-focal point along γ, then it is a bifurcation instant for (S0, γ ), and one of the following alternatives occurs: 

(iii-1) There exists a sequence of distinct C3 Euler-Lagrange curves of L emanating perpen-dicularly from S0 and ending at γ(μ), αk : [0 , μ ] → M , αk̸ = γ|[0 ,μ ], k = 1 , 2, · · · ,such that αk → γ|[0 ,μ ] in C2([0 , μ ], RN ) as k → ∞ .

emanating perpendicularly from S0 and ending at γ(λ), αλ : [0 , λ ] → M , αλ̸ = γ|[0 ,λ ],such that ∥αλ − γ|[0 ,λ ]∥C2([0 ,λ ],RN ) → 0 as λ → μ.

As noted in Remark 2.8, when M is an open subset in Rn the conditions in the above theorems may be weakened suitably. 

Remark 1.25. Clearly, if the Lagrangian L in Assumption 1.20 comes from a family of C6

Riemannian metrics {hλ | λ ∈ Λ} on M , i.e., L(λ, t, x, v ) = ( hλ)x(v, v ) for all ( λ, t, x, v ), as direct consequences of the above results we immediately obtain many bifurcation theorems of geodesics on Riemannian manifolds. See [23, Part B]. 

Remark 1.26. A natural question is how to verify the conditions required in Theorems 1.6, 1.15, 1.19, and 1.24. We address this question in Section 6 with Appendix B. 16 Guangcun Lu 

1.9 Organization of the article 

Section 2 introduces the basic notation and presents some technical lemmas that will be used in the subsequent sections. In Section 3, we discuss bifurcations of Lagrangian system trajectories connecting two sub-manifolds. By reducing the problem to Euclidean spaces, we prove the main results presented in Section 1.5, namely, Theorems 1.4, 1.5, 1.6, and 1.9. The proof of an important lemma, Lemma 3.1, is deferred to Appendix A. In Section 4, we study bifurcations of Lagrangian trajectories with endpoints related by an isometry. The main results of Section 1.6—Theorems 1.13, 1.14 and 1.15—are proved by a reduction to Euclidean spaces. Section 5 deals with bifurcations of brake orbits in Lagrangian systems. Based on a reduction to Euclidean spaces (using Claim A.1, to be proved in Appendix A), we prove the main results of Section 1.8: Theorems 1.22, 1.23, and 1.24. In Section 6, using the abstract results in Appendix B, we derive more readily applicable corollaries of the main results. We then apply them to bifurcation problems concerning physical Lagrangians with potential and electromagnetic forces, specifically presenting bifurcation results for the planar forced simple pendulum. Appendix A provides the proofs of Lemma 3.1 and Claim A.1. In Appendix B, we study the dependence on parameters of the Morse indices of a family of abstract functionals defined on a separable real Hilbert space at a common critical point. 

Acknowledgements. I would like to thank the anonymous referee for his/her many valuable comments and suggestions regarding the mathematical content and the writing, which have greatly improved the revised version. 

# 2 Preliminaries and notation 

This section collects the standard notations, function spaces, and basic technical lemmas used throughout the paper. It aims to make the paper self-contained and to clarify the meaning of symbols introduced in subsequent sections. 

2.1 Notation and Conventions 

• Vectors in Rm are understood as column vectors; ( ·, ·)Rm and | · | denote, respectively, the standard Euclidean inner product and norm in Rm.

• The transpose of a matrix M is denoted by M ⊤.

• For a Hilbert space H, Ls(H) denotes the space of continuous linear self-adjoint operators on H. We also use Ls(Rm) to denote the set of real symmetric matrices of order m). 

• For normed (real) linear spaces X and Y , L(X, Y ) is the space of continuous linear map-pings from X to Y . Call X∗ := L(X, R) the dual (or adjoint) space of X.

• For a map f from normed (real) linear spaces X to Y , let Df (x) denote the Gˆ ateaux derivative of f at x ∈ X, and let df (x) (or f ′(x)) denotes the Fr´ echet derivative of f at 

x ∈ X. Both are elements of the space L(X, Y ). We may also use the notation f ′(x) for the Gˆ ateaux derivative Df (x) when no confusion arises. Bifurcations for Lagrangian systems and geodesics I 17 

• For a real functional f on a Hilbert space H, the the derivative f ′(x) of f at x ∈ H belongs to the dual space H∗. By the Riesz representation theorem, f ′(x) corresponds to a unique element in H, which we call the gradient of f at x, denoted by ∇f (x). The Fr´ echet (or Gˆ ateaux) derivative of ∇f at x ∈ H is denoted by f ′′ (x). This is an element of Ls(H). More precisely, f ′′ (x) is identified with the second derivative (f ′)′(x) ∈ L(H; H∗), which corresponds to a symmetric bilinear form on H via the Riesz representation theorem (identifying H∗ with H). This is equivalent to the derivative 

D(∇f )( x). 

• Lp([0 , τ ]; Rm) (1 ≤ p < ∞) denotes the space of (equivalence classes of) p-integrable functions from [0 , τ ] to Rm, equipped with the norm ∥u∥p = ( R τ

# 4 Proofs of Theorems 1.13, 1.14, 1.15 

The proofs are completely similar to those of Section 3. We only outline main procedures.

# 6 Corollaries and examples 

In this section, we first derive some corollaries of the main results using the abstract framework in Appendix B, as these corollaries are more readily applicable. We then apply these results to physical Lagrangians—such as those involving potential and electromagnetic forces—and finally present bifurcation results for the planar forced simple pendulum. 

6.1 Corollaries 

Assumption 6.1. Let ( M, g, Ig) be as in Assumption 1.0 in Introduction. For a real τ > 0, consider a function W ∈ C2([0 , τ ] × M, R), and a C2 Lagrangian L(t, q, v ) on [0 , τ ] × T M that is strictly convex with respect to v. In summary, the above discussion indicates that for a sufficiently smooth Lagrangian function that is strictly convex fiberwise, the corresponding Lagrangian system admits a perturbation of the Lagrangian function near a solution at which the action functional has a non-vanishing nullity, such that a Rabinowitz-type bifurcation occurs near that solution. The results analogous to Theorems 6.8 and 6.9 can be readily formulated. We omit them. Instead, we consider a concrete example. Bifurcations for Lagrangian systems and geodesics I 63 

6.2 Example: planar simple pendulum 

Consider the planar simple pendulum equation: ¨u + gl sin u = 0 , (6.7) where g is the universal gravitational constant, l is the length of the pendulum, and one end of the pendulum is fixed at the origin. It is well known that there are two kinds of nontrivial motions of this planar simple pendulum: rotations around the origin and oscillations. The linearized equation of (6.7) at the zero solution is l¨u(t) + gu (t) = 0, which has the general solution u = C1 cos( ωt ) + C2 sin( ωt ), where ω =

q gl . These solutions have period T := 2πω .

T -periodic solutions of (6.7) are critical points of the functional Φ( u) =

el(−t) = el(t). Summarizing these (A.6) is proved.

# B Morse indexes of a class of abstract functionals 

Let H be a separable real Hilbert space with inner product ( ·, ·), and let Fsa (H) denote the set of all bounded linear self-adjoint Fredholm operators on H. For a C0 path t 7 → Bt ∈ F sa (H), 

t ∈ (−η, η ), we have a family of functionals on H,

ft(x) = 12 (Btx, x ), x ∈ H, 

for which the origin 0 ∈ H is a critical point with finite Morse index. Suppose that dim ker B0 =

N > 0 and t 7 → Bt is differentiable at 0. The derivative of Bt at t = 0, denoted by ˙B0, belongs to Ls(H). Consider the symmetric bilinear form Q on ker B0 given by 

Q(x, y ) = ddt (x, B t(y)) t=0 = ( x, ˙B0(y)) , x, y ∈ ker B0.

The following result is contained in the proof of [8, Lemma 3.23]. For the sake of completeness, we present a detailed proof.

(B.1) is proved. Let B ∈ F sa (H), and let ⟨· , ·⟩ be an alternative inner product on H that induces a norm equivalent to the one induced by ( ·, ·). Since ⟨· , ·⟩ is bounded and coercive with respect to the original norm, the Lax–Milgram theorem implies that there exists a bounded linear invertible operator Ξ : H → H such that for all u, v ∈ H,

⟨u, v ⟩ = (Ξ u, v ) and hence ⟨Ξ−1u, v ⟩ = ( u, v ). (B.7) 

Claim B.2. The operator Ξ−1B is also Fredholm, and self-adjoint with respect to the inner product ⟨· , ·⟩ .

Proof. The first claim is clear since Ξ (and consequently Ξ −1) is bounded and invertible. To prove the second one, let (Ξ −1B)∗ denote the adjoint operator of Ξ −1B with respect to the inner product ⟨· , ·⟩ . Then for any u, v ∈ H,

⟨(Ξ −1B)∗u, v ⟩ = ⟨u, Ξ−1Bv ⟩ = ⟨Ξ−1Bv, u ⟩ = ( Bv, u ) = ( Bu, v ) = ⟨Ξ−1Bu, v ⟩,

where the third and the final equalities come from (B.7). Hence (Ξ −1B)∗ = Ξ −1B, i.e., Ξ −1B is self-adjoint with respect to ⟨· , ·⟩ .As a consequence of Claim B.2 and Proposition B.1, we have: 

Corollary B.3. Under the above assumptions, suppose that Q is non-degenerate and has the Morse index m−(Q) = q. Then there exists 0 < δ 0 < η such that 

m−(ft, 0) =
